<li id="cite_note-Richards1995-2-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Richards1995-2_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFRichards1995">Richards, John F. (1995), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=HHyVh29gy4QC&amp;pg=PA2" rel="nofollow"><i>The Mughal Empire</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, p. 2, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-56603-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-56603-2"><bdi>978-0-521-56603-2</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Mughal+Empire&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1995&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-56603-2&amp;rft.aulast=Richards&amp;rft.aufirst=John+F.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DHHyVh29gy4QC%26pg%3DPA2&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "Although the first two Timurid emperors and many of their noblemen were recent migrants to the subcontinent, the dynasty and the empire itself became indisputably Indian. The interests and futures of all concerned were in India, not in ancestral homelands in the Middle East or Central Asia. Furthermore, the Mughal empire emerged from the Indian historical experience. It was the end product of a millennium of Muslim conquest, colonization, and state-building in the Indian subcontinent."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Stein2010-12-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010-12_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFStein2010"><a href="/wiki/Burton_Stein" title="Burton Stein">Stein, Burton</a> (2010), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QY4zdTDwMAQC&amp;pg=PA159" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, John Wiley &amp; Sons, pp. 159–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1"><bdi>978-1-4443-2351-1</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=159-&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4443-2351-1&amp;rft.aulast=Stein&amp;rft.aufirst=Burton&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DQY4zdTDwMAQC%26pg%3DPA159&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "The realm so defined and governed was a vast territory of some 750,000 square miles [1,900,000 km<sup>2</sup>], ranging from the frontier with Central Asia in northern Afghanistan to the northern uplands of the Deccan plateau, and from the Indus basin on the west to the Assamese highlands in the east."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Gilbert2017-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gilbert2017_14-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFGilbert2017">Gilbert, Marc Jason (2017), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1dhKDgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA75" rel="nofollow"><i>South Asia in World History</i></a>, Oxford University Press, pp. 75–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-066137-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-066137-3"><bdi>978-0-19-066137-3</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=South+Asia+in+World+History&amp;rft.pages=75-&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2017&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-066137-3&amp;rft.aulast=Gilbert&amp;rft.aufirst=Marc+Jason&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D1dhKDgAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA75&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "Babur then adroitly gave the Ottomans his promise not to attack them in return for their military aid, which he received in the form of the newest of battlefield inventions, the matchlock gun and cast cannons, as well as instructors to train his men to use them."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Stein2010-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010_15-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFStein2010"><a href="/wiki/Burton_Stein" title="Burton Stein">Stein, Burton</a> (2010), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QY4zdTDwMAQC&amp;pg=PA159" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, John Wiley &amp; Sons, pp. 159–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1"><bdi>978-1-4443-2351-1</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=159-&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4443-2351-1&amp;rft.aulast=Stein&amp;rft.aufirst=Burton&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DQY4zdTDwMAQC%26pg%3DPA159&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "Another possible date for the beginning of the Mughal regime is 1600, when the institutions that defined the regime were set firmly in place and when the heartland of the empire was defined; both of these were the accomplishment of Babur’s grandson Akbar."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Stein2010-1-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010-1_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFStein2010"><a href="/wiki/Burton_Stein" title="Burton Stein">Stein, Burton</a> (2010), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QY4zdTDwMAQC&amp;pg=PA159" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, John Wiley &amp; Sons, pp. 159–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1"><bdi>978-1-4443-2351-1</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=159-&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4443-2351-1&amp;rft.aulast=Stein&amp;rft.aufirst=Burton&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DQY4zdTDwMAQC%26pg%3DPA159&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "The imperial career of the Mughal house is conventionally reckoned to have ended in 1707 when the emperor Aurangzeb, a fifth-generation descendant of Babur, died. His fifty-year reign began in 1658 with the Mughal state seeming as strong as ever or even stronger. But in Aurangzeb’s later years the state was brought to the brink of destruction, over which it toppled within a decade and a half after his death; by 1720 imperial Mughal rule was largely finished and an epoch of two imperial centuries had closed."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Richards1995-3-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Richards1995-3_17-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFRichards1995">Richards, John F. (1995), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=HHyVh29gy4QC&amp;pg=PAxv" rel="nofollow"><i>The Mughal Empire</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, p. xv, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-56603-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-56603-2"><bdi>978-0-521-56603-2</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Mughal+Empire&amp;rft.pages=xv&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1995&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-56603-2&amp;rft.aulast=Richards&amp;rft.aufirst=John+F.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DHHyVh29gy4QC%26pg%3DPAxv&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "By the latter date (1720) the essential structure of the centralized state was disintegrated beyond repair."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Stein2010-2-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010-2_18-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFStein2010"><a href="/wiki/Burton_Stein" title="Burton Stein">Stein, Burton</a> (2010), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QY4zdTDwMAQC&amp;pg=PA159" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, John Wiley &amp; Sons, pp. 159–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1"><bdi>978-1-4443-2351-1</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=159-&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4443-2351-1&amp;rft.aulast=Stein&amp;rft.aufirst=Burton&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DQY4zdTDwMAQC%26pg%3DPA159&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "The vaunting of such progenitors pointed up the central character of the Mughal regime as a warrior state: it was born in war and it was sustained by war until the eighteenth century, when warfare destroyed it."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Robb2011-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Robb2011_19-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFRobb2011">Robb, Peter (2011), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=GQ-2VH1LO_EC&amp;pg=PA108" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, Macmillan, pp. 108–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-230-34549-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-230-34549-2"><bdi>978-0-230-34549-2</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=108-&amp;rft.pub=Macmillan&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-230-34549-2&amp;rft.aulast=Robb&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DGQ-2VH1LO_EC%26pg%3DPA108&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "The Mughal state was geared for war, and succeeded while it won its battles.  It controlled territory partly through its network of strongholds, from its fortified capitals in Agra, Delhi or Lahore, which defined its heartlands, to the converted and expanded forts of Rajasthan and the Deccan. The emperors' will was frequently enforced in battle. Hundreds of army scouts were an important source of information. But the empire's administrative structure too was defined by and directed at war. Local military checkpoints or thanas kept order. Directly appointed imperial military and civil commanders (faujdars) controlled the cavalry and infantry, or the administration, in each region. The peasantry in turn were often armed, able to provide supporters for regional powers, and liable to rebellion on their own account: continual pacification was required of the rulers."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Gilbert2017-2-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gilbert2017-2_20-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFGilbert2017">Gilbert, Marc Jason (2017), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1dhKDgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA75" rel="nofollow"><i>South Asia in World History</i></a>, Oxford University Press, pp. 75–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-066137-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-066137-3"><bdi>978-0-19-066137-3</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=South+Asia+in+World+History&amp;rft.pages=75-&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2017&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-066137-3&amp;rft.aulast=Gilbert&amp;rft.aufirst=Marc+Jason&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D1dhKDgAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA75&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "With Safavid and Ottoman aid, the Mughals would soon join these two powers in a triumvirate of warrior-driven, expansionist, and both militarily and bureaucratically efficient early modern states, now often called "gunpowder empires" due to their common proficiency is using such weapons to conquer lands they sought to control."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFAsherTalbot2006">Asher, Catherine B.; Talbot, Cynthia (2006), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ZvaGuaJIJgoC&amp;pg=PA115" rel="nofollow"><i>India Before Europe</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, pp. 115–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7"><bdi>978-0-521-80904-7</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=India+Before+Europe&amp;rft.pages=115-&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-80904-7&amp;rft.aulast=Asher&amp;rft.aufirst=Catherine+B.&amp;rft.au=Talbot%2C+Cynthia&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DZvaGuaJIJgoC%26pg%3DPA115&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFRobb2011">Robb, Peter (2011), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=GQ-2VH1LO_EC&amp;pg=PA99" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, Macmillan, pp. 99–100, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-230-34549-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-230-34549-2"><bdi>978-0-230-34549-2</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=99-100&amp;rft.pub=Macmillan&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-230-34549-2&amp;rft.aulast=Robb&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DGQ-2VH1LO_EC%26pg%3DPA99&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-2-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-2_23-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-2_23-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-2_23-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFAsherTalbot2006">Asher, Catherine B.; Talbot, Cynthia (2006), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ZvaGuaJIJgoC&amp;pg=PA152" rel="nofollow"><i>India Before Europe</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, pp. 152–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7"><bdi>978-0-521-80904-7</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=India+Before+Europe&amp;rft.pages=152-&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-80904-7&amp;rft.aulast=Asher&amp;rft.aufirst=Catherine+B.&amp;rft.au=Talbot%2C+Cynthia&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DZvaGuaJIJgoC%26pg%3DPA152&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Stein2010-3-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010-3_24-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010-3_24-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFStein2010"><a href="/wiki/Burton_Stein" title="Burton Stein">Stein, Burton</a> (2010), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QY4zdTDwMAQC&amp;pg=PA164" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, John Wiley &amp; Sons, pp. 164–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1"><bdi>978-1-4443-2351-1</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=164-&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4443-2351-1&amp;rft.aulast=Stein&amp;rft.aufirst=Burton&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DQY4zdTDwMAQC%26pg%3DPA164&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "The resource base of Akbar’s new order was land revenue"</span>

<li id="cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-1-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-1_25-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-1_25-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFAsherTalbot2006">Asher, Catherine B.; Talbot, Cynthia (2006), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ZvaGuaJIJgoC&amp;pg=PA152" rel="nofollow"><i>India Before Europe</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, pp. 158–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7"><bdi>978-0-521-80904-7</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=India+Before+Europe&amp;rft.pages=158-&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-80904-7&amp;rft.aulast=Asher&amp;rft.aufirst=Catherine+B.&amp;rft.au=Talbot%2C+Cynthia&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DZvaGuaJIJgoC%26pg%3DPA152&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "The Mughal empire was based in the interior of a large land-mass and derived the vast majority of its revenues from agriculture."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Stein2010-4-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010-4_26-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Stein2010-4_26-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFStein2010"><a href="/wiki/Burton_Stein" title="Burton Stein">Stein, Burton</a> (2010), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QY4zdTDwMAQC&amp;pg=PA159" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of India</i></a>, John Wiley &amp; Sons, pp. 164–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4443-2351-1"><bdi>978-1-4443-2351-1</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+India&amp;rft.pages=164-&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4443-2351-1&amp;rft.aulast=Stein&amp;rft.aufirst=Burton&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DQY4zdTDwMAQC%26pg%3DPA159&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "... well over half of the output from the fields in his realm, after the costs of production had been met, is estimated to have been taken from the peasant producers by way of official taxes and unofficial exactions. Moreover, payments were exacted in money, and this required a well regulated silver currency."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-3-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-3_27-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-3_27-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFAsherTalbot2006">Asher, Catherine B.; Talbot, Cynthia (2006), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ZvaGuaJIJgoC&amp;pg=PA152" rel="nofollow"><i>India Before Europe</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, pp. 152–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7"><bdi>978-0-521-80904-7</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=India+Before+Europe&amp;rft.pages=152-&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-80904-7&amp;rft.aulast=Asher&amp;rft.aufirst=Catherine+B.&amp;rft.au=Talbot%2C+Cynthia&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DZvaGuaJIJgoC%26pg%3DPA152&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "His stipulation that land taxes be paid in cash forced peasants into market networks, where they could obtain the necessary money, while the standardization of imperial currency made the exchange of goods for money easier."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-4-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-4_28-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFAsherTalbot2006">Asher, Catherine B.; Talbot, Cynthia (2006), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ZvaGuaJIJgoC&amp;pg=PA152" rel="nofollow"><i>India Before Europe</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, pp. 152–, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-80904-7"><bdi>978-0-521-80904-7</bdi></a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=India+Before+Europe&amp;rft.pages=152-&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-80904-7&amp;rft.aulast=Asher&amp;rft.aufirst=Catherine+B.&amp;rft.au=Talbot%2C+Cynthia&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DZvaGuaJIJgoC%26pg%3DPA152&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span> Quote: "Above all, the long period of relative peace ushered in by Akbar's power, and maintained by his successors, contributed to India's economic expansion."</span>

<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFRichard_M._Eaton2013">Richard M. Eaton (2013). <i>Expanding Frontiers in South Asian and World History Essays in Honour of John F. Richards</i>. Cambridge University Press. p. 21. <q>I consider all this army (Marathas) as my own and I will get my work done through them. It is necessary to take our hands off Malwa. God willing, I will enter into an understanding with them and entrust the Mulukgiri(raiding) on that side of the Narmada to them.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Expanding+Frontiers+in+South+Asian+and+World+History+Essays+in+Honour+of+John+F.+Richards&amp;rft.pages=21&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.au=Richard+M.+Eaton&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.google.ca/books/edition/Annals_of_the_Bhandarkar_Oriental_Resear/p5VYH7FhoTsC?hl=en&amp;gbpv=1&amp;bsq=It+is+necessary+to+take+our+hands+off+Malwa.+God+willing,+I+will+enter+into+an+understanding+with+them&amp;dq=It+is+necessary+to+take+our+hands+off+Malwa.+God+willing,+I+will+enter+into+an+understanding+with+them&amp;printsec=frontcover" rel="nofollow"><i>Annals of the Bhandarkar Oriental Research Institute, Poona: Volumes 51-53</i></a>. Bhandarkar Oriental Research Institute. 1970. p. 94. <q>The Mughal court was hostile to Nizam-ul-Mulk. If it had the power, it would have crushed him. To save himself from the hostile intentions of the Emperor, the Nizam did not interfere with the Maratha activities in Malwa and Gujarat. As revealed in the anecdotes narrated b Lala Mansaram, the Nizam-ul-Mulk considered the Maratha army operating in Malwa and Gujarat as his own</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Annals+of+the+Bhandarkar+Oriental+Research+Institute%2C+Poona%3A+Volumes+51-53&amp;rft.pages=94&amp;rft.pub=Bhandarkar+Oriental+Research+Institute&amp;rft.date=1970&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.ca%2Fbooks%2Fedition%2FAnnals_of_the_Bhandarkar_Oriental_Resear%2Fp5VYH7FhoTsC%3Fhl%3Den%26gbpv%3D1%26bsq%3DIt%2Bis%2Bnecessary%2Bto%2Btake%2Bour%2Bhands%2Boff%2BMalwa.%2BGod%2Bwilling%2C%2BI%2Bwill%2Benter%2Binto%2Ban%2Bunderstanding%2Bwith%2Bthem%26dq%3DIt%2Bis%2Bnecessary%2Bto%2Btake%2Bour%2Bhands%2Boff%2BMalwa.%2BGod%2Bwilling%2C%2BI%2Bwill%2Benter%2Binto%2Ban%2Bunderstanding%2Bwith%2Bthem%26printsec%3Dfrontcover&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMughal+Empire"></span></span>
</li>
